        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer881503600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7856153338924578281">_________________<br/><b> FAMOUS </b><br/>_________________<br/>I remember when the twins mentioned creating this series and how excited I was to know I would be able to continue reading about <b>my favorite famous families</b>. The Hales, Meadows, and Cobalts, from the <i>Addicted</i> series, are now parents with their children are growing up in the limelight. Some of the kids are now young adults and the world wants a piece of them. <br/><br/>_________________<br/><b>MOFFY</b><br/>_________________<br/><b>Moffy</b> is Lily & Lo's 22-year-old son. He lives with his co</span>
  <span id="freeText7856153338924578281" style="display:none">_________________<br><b> FAMOUS </b><br>_________________<br>I remember when the twins mentioned creating this series and how excited I was to know I would be able to continue reading about <b>my favorite famous families</b>. The Hales, Meadows, and Cobalts, from the <i>Addicted</i> series, are now parents with their children are growing up in the limelight. Some of the kids are now young adults and the world wants a piece of them. <br><br>_________________<br><b>MOFFY</b><br>_________________<br><b>Moffy</b> is Lily &amp; Lo's 22-year-old son. He lives with his cousin, Jane Cobalt, and because of who their parents are they have 24/7 bodyguards. Moffy is sought have by the paparazzi and his adoring fans. <br><br>_________________<br><b>FARROW</b><br>_________________<br><b>Farrow</b> is the 27-year-old bodyguard to Lily for the last 3 years. When Moffy's bodyguard retires Lily suggest that Farrow be the one to take that position. As with any mother they want the very best for their kids and Farrow fits that bill. <br><br>_________________<br><b>DAMAGED</b><br>_________________<br>Being the kids of a famous family isn't always easy especially when your life is lived in the public eye. Everyone, family &amp; public, knows Moffy is bi-sexual. He has the public watching to see if he'll be a sex addict like his mom or a drunk like his father. Even though his parents conquered their demons the public is waiting for him to slip up and show them that he is also <b>damaged </b>like his parents.<br><br>_________________<br><b>LIKE</b><br>_________________<br>Farrow has been around the Hale family long before he became their bodyguard. As a kid, his father was the family doctor and is still their family doctor. Farrow tagged along on calls to the Hale household because his dad was priming him to follow in the long generational tradition of becoming a doctor. Moffy had a crush on Farrow all those years so when Farrow became his bodyguard the two of them postured on who was in charge. Since we are privy to both POVs, we know that Farrow<b> likes</b> Moffy too. <br><br>_________________<br><b>US</b><br>_________________<br>These two alphas have to learn how to be together without anyone finding out. If Farrow became famous then he won't be able to protect Moffy anymore. Being just<b> "us"</b> with each other when they could find a free moment was touching. Seeing how Moffy reacts to his first long-term relationship was endearing. The little things they do for each other were sweet. <br><br><br><b>DAMAGED LIKE US</b> is the first book in the<u> Like Us</u> series. <i>"The Like Us series is a true series, one continuous timeline, that follows a family of wealthy celebrities and the people that protect them. Damaged Like Us can be read and enjoyed without reading any of Krista &amp; Becca's other novels."</i> <b>Lovers of forbidden romance will enjoy this m/m romance.</b> The story is a real page-turner that will keep you up reading late into the night!<br><br><br><a href="http://foxyblogs.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1442610494i/16258382._SX540_.jpg" width="400" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><b>Follow Foxy Blogs at:</b> <a href="http://foxyblogs.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> ♥ <a href="https://twitter.com/FoxyBlogs" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ♥ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/foxyblogs/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ♥ <a href="https://www.facebook.com/FoxyBlogs/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7856153338924578281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2169715473" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169715473" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8429172-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595453256p2/8429172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2169715473?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/8429172-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2169715473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8921815884042813124">|3.5 stars|<br/><br/><br/>Diving into the book I didn't know what to expect. I knew I missed the core six with all my heart but I was also aware this was not about them so separating that from what I really wanted was difficult at first and I found myself wondering when were Lily, Lo and the rest.<br/><br/>And while I enjoyed this book a lot, I didn't do it for the main couple. All the characters -The Hales, Meadows, Cobalts and the bodyguards were so damn interesting, I couldn't help but needing more of them and less o</span>
  <span id="freeText8921815884042813124" style="display:none">|3.5 stars|<br /><br /><br />Diving into the book I didn't know what to expect. I knew I missed the core six with all my heart but I was also aware this was not about them so separating that from what I really wanted was difficult at first and I found myself wondering when were Lily, Lo and the rest.<br /><br />And while I enjoyed this book a lot, I didn't do it for the main couple. All the characters -The Hales, Meadows, Cobalts and the bodyguards were so damn interesting, I couldn't help but needing more of them and less of Maximoff and Farrow. <br /><br />I don't know if it's because I found the couple kinda boring. Cute and hot but boring or because the twins created characters that demanded so much attention while having so little time.<br /><br />I loved Maximoff and Farrow as individuals and how they interacted with the rest of the characters but most of what they did was having sex and while we got to know Moffy, in the end, I didn't know who Farrow really was.<br /><br />I guess we go deeply into the couple in the next book but I'm more interested in Jane and the rest of the family right now. So, while I want to read and going to read the next books, I can't deny the fact that I don't want them to be about Farrow and Moffy. Or at least I need more about them without the sex. Let me know Farrow. Let me see how he interacts with all of the family and the guards.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8921815884042813124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1464988903" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1464988903" />
    <a title="prerna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48184488-prerna"><img alt="prerna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495800930p2/48184488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1464988903?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prerna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prerna" href="/user/show/48184488-prerna">prerna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48184488-prerna?shelf=dont-care-or-lost-interest">dont-care-or-lost-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48184488-prerna?shelf=overrated-or-overhyped-af">overrated-or-overhyped-af</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48184488-prerna?shelf=worst-ending-ever">worst-ending-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48184488-prerna?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48184488-prerna?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48184488-prerna?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48184488-prerna?shelf=why-did-i-bother">why-did-i-bother</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1464988903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13395063944919413979"><b>1.5/5</b><br/><br/>(There <i>are</i> spoilers, but only Addicted spoilers are hidden)<br/><br/>Alright let's gooo. <br/><br/><b>1. The Hale Propaganda</b><br/>Really, I've always had a feeling that despite K&B saying otherwise, the Hales (Lily & Lo) were clearly their favourite. And that's okay, I understand they were the original characters so they probably are more attached to them. But what's <i>not</i> okay is other characters suffering just for their benefit. Throughout Addicted the others (Connor & Rose, Daisy & Ryke) always, ALWAYS, put Lily and L</span>
  <span id="freeText13395063944919413979" style="display:none"><b>1.5/5</b><br /><br />(There <i>are</i> spoilers, but only Addicted spoilers are hidden)<br /><br />Alright let's gooo. <br /><br /><b>1. The Hale Propaganda</b><br />Really, I've always had a feeling that despite K&amp;B saying otherwise, the Hales (Lily &amp; Lo) were clearly their favourite. And that's okay, I understand they were the original characters so they probably are more attached to them. But what's <i>not</i> okay is other characters suffering just for their benefit. Throughout Addicted the others (Connor &amp; Rose, Daisy &amp; Ryke) always, ALWAYS, put Lily and Lo above their own happiness, and it always irked me because Lily and Lo never really did that for anyone (besides each other, but that's a whole new argument about their codependent relationship).<br /><br />But in DLU this went on to a whole new level and I am NOT okay with it.<br /><br />Firstly, I get that we're in Moffy's pov and he loves his family, but after the first few hundred time, the "Hales are the Best" promotion becomes quite stale and boring, and frankly, very annoying. Especially when you keep telling me, but you don't <i>show</i> me anything to back it up. Not to mention putting Moffy on a pedestal. He was some great sibling, and an even greater cousin. Everyone looked up to him. He was just all around an amazing guy. But how? We get told all of this, but we’re never really shown much. It was infuriating.<br /><br />This book was way too focused on Moffy and Farrow’s relationship, there was no space for anything else. This book didn’t even seem to have much of a plot, it was just relationship development (which I think was also done quite poorly; it was too sudden and rushed, and by that I mean the entire time it just felt too… sexualised? Though all of a sudden it’s not another NSA for Moffy, it’s something more? We didn’t see much, but whatever), and maybe it’s my fault that I really expected to see more of the LU kids. I wanted to meet them and see their relationship with Moffy, but we didn’t get anything. Instead we got dicks hardening faster than I could turn the page.<br /><br />Secondly, was the whole thing with Moffy and Ryke necessary? In SKOP Moffy was a child (I think around 12?) and it made sense then when he had doubts and he wanted to make his dad proud, and he wanted everyone to know how much he loved his dad; that he was Loren Hale’s son, not Ryke Meadows. That was understandable, and I don’t remember the details but it was eventually resolved, and Moffy resumed his relationship with Ryke, rather than cutting him out of his life. That was the end, or it should have been.<br /><br />In DLU Moffy is a grown ass man, he has apparently been close to Ryke for years, Ryke practically taught him everything from camping to riding a bike.<br /><br /><i>Exhibit A:</i><br />My dad raised me, and when I was twelve, I had a choice. I could either resent Ryke or I could love him as much as my dad does.<br />I chose to love him. As a teenager, he taught me how to ride a motorcycle. We went on annual camping trips. I created the Charity Camp-Away out of my love for hiking, camping, kayaking—and would that even exist without Ryke?<br />He showed me how to build a fire with flint. How to pitch a tent. How to climb rock faces. Outside of the Meadows family, I’m the only one who’s ever been to their Costa Rica cabin-treehouse.<br /><br />After everything, after <i>years</i> of this, due to stupid rumours that Moffy knows won’t change, he decides that he can’t be like Ryke at all. Not only that, but he treats him quite poorly. I don’t know about you, but by Hothouse Flower I was quite literally Done with how the Hale men treated Ryke, so this only further incensed me.<br /><br /><i>Exhibit B:</i><br />“You know my mom was on the front page of Celebrity Crush this morning?” My shoulders are locked. “The headline: Lily Calloway Goes Back to Her Old Wild Ways! They had a photograph of her sticking her hand down my dad’s pants. And Uncle Ryke is upset over a cover where he’s scaling a mountain during a damn sunrise.”<br />A bad, acidic taste drips down my throat, but I don’t look away.<br /><br /><i>Exhibit C:</i><br />I’ve noticed he’s been ditching most of his green shirts for red. A deliberate, calculated change.<br />The public associates most of the Hales, Meadows, and Cobalts with their favorite colors.<br />And his dad’s is red.<br />Ryke’s is green.<br /><br />It’s just??? Colour???? Of clothing??<br /><br /><i>Exhibit D:</i><br />Then in a different language, she asks, “Has pensado en la ultra?” Have you thought about the ultra?<br />Ryke Meadows taught his daughters to speak Spanish. And he taught me. I’m proud to be fluent, but in the past year, being constantly compared to Ryke…I don’t know.<br />I question everything.<br /><br /><i>Exhibit E:</i><br />If she asked me a year ago, I wouldn’t have hesitated like I do now.<br />“It’s because my dad ran an ultra, isn’t it?”<br />“Sul.” I rub my sharpened jaw. “If I go, they’ll compare me more to your dad than they do now.”<br /><br />This is self-explanatory, I don’t think anything else needs to be said. But it was grating and annoying, and absolutely awful. I’m tired of this. Ryke deserved better.<br /><br /><b>2. The Hale Propaganda: part deux</b><br /><br />(This is my favourite by the way!)<br /><br />The great Moffy Hales y’all:<br /><br /><i>Maximoff smiles throughout the emo-punk song. “Tom.” He shakes his head and then finds a moment to glance at me. “He was only ten when I finally told everyone that I liked girls and guys, and I didn’t think it’d matter to him. But I stood in front of my family at Christmas, presents half-unwrapped, with goddamn Jack Frost playing in the background—and when everyone started hugging me and smiling, I looked over and Tom was crying.”</i><br /><br />AND<br /><br /><i>“He was happy.”<br />“So goddamn happy.” Maximoff blinks back water that wells. “Tom knew he was gay…for as long as I can remember, and I’m five years older than him. And when I knelt in front of him and hugged him—I felt guilty.” He cringes. “For not telling him sooner. I pretty much knew I was attracted to guys by thirteen. That’s two years where I could’ve told him.”<br />I extend my arm over the back of his seat, acting like I’m using the seat to check behind us. I just want to be closer to Maximoff. “It’s admirable how much you care,” I say, “but he’s lucky he has you at all.” Warmly, I add, “Your compassion is showing.”</i><br /><br />How compassionate. I’m literally crying, there are angry tears in my eyes. I mean, Moffy really did That for Tom 😩😩👏🏽👏🏽<br /><br />But listen to this: Tom was 10 when this happened, and Moffy deadass felt guilty for not telling Tom sooner. <b>Except Tom was completely and utterly okay with his sexuality when he was s e v e n!</b><br /><br />Case in point:<br /><br />Tom takes a peek at the lifeguard stand. “What if he’s really cute?”<br /><br />We’re not suddenly surprised that Tom is attracted to boys and not girls. <b>Rose and Connor cultivated this safe space for their children. Inclusive of just about everything and fucking anything. So when Tom started feeling an attraction towards guys, he didn’t make a speech. He didn’t worry his parents would disown him or fucking hate him or try to convince him to love someone he can’t.</b><br /><br />– Some Kind of Perfect.<br /><br />But it was Moffy who did that for Tom, right? Not his own parents? Gotta love the Hales :)))<br /><br /><b>3. The Writing &amp; Characterisation &amp; POV</b><br />How many times can one read about razor sharp cheekbones (this coming from the very first Addicted book) before it becomes repetitive and unoriginal??<br /><br />Why did both Moffy and Farrow get hard every other paragraph?? Farrow was literally listing supplies for a piercing for Kinney’s birthday, and Moffy got hard?? Is that necessary or realistic?<br /><br />The writing from the first Addicted book to SKOP had improved so much, but this? I don’t know what to call this. It was quite terrible, a huge step backwards for K&amp;B and quite frankly, a big disappointment.<br /><br />Other than the writing the characters were so off. Not only were they OOC, but also separate. I don’t know how else to describe it, but the relationship we saw between the LU kids in SKOP is not what we got here. I understand that they were much younger in SKOP, but even between siblings it didn’t feel like they were close at all. I know everyone loved Moffy and Jane’s relationship, but I couldn’t see it. Again, we were told in words how close they were, they said it themselves, but we weren’t shown much, not like we were shown in SKOP and previous books. <br /><br />Moffy himself was quite OOC too, and on that note, his POV characters sounded like a mix of both Loren and Luka Kotova’s pov. He didn’t really seem to have his own voice. And his obsession with wanting to become 100% Loren Hale didn’t help it either. Moffy started off sounding exactly like Loren Hale, and throughout the novel he became more like Luka. Since I didn’t enjoy either of their pov’s much, I’m not that surprised this was a huge let down.<br /><br /><b>4. Chapter 40 and 41 – Very Out of Character</b><br />The last thing to really cement my dislike for this book.<br /><br />What the hell was <i>that</i>? <br />Firstly, it was disgusting, this White plot twist.<br />Secondly, it did nothing but cheapen EVERYONE’S relationships (especially Moffy &amp; Jane’s, and their relationship with their parents/aunts/uncles).<br /><br />Despite everything, Moffy and Jane both didn’t deserve this shit storyline. And they especially didn’t deserve their own parents turning on them. Which is just unbelievable. None of them would ever, <i>ever</i> pull the shit they did in DLU in Addicted. It was the ugliest out of character shit I’ve seen in a long time.<br /><br />The parents, who have dealt with false rumours and lies for years by now, they really believed that disgusting rumour about Moffy and Jane? Lmao. <br />Am I honestly meant to take this shit seriously???<br /><br />I have no love lost for Loren Hale, but do K&amp;B really expect me to believe that Loren would question his own son, after he himself was in a similar position with his dad? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[You know,, those rumours about Jonathan sexually abusing him? And no one believed Loren? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />My heart literally broke when: “Nous avons besoin d'explications, mon coeur.” <i>We need explanations, my heart.</i><br /><br />No, you do not. You do not need any fucking explanations. This isn’t you. You would never do this. What the fuck. A stake to my heart would’ve been more real than this bullshit.<br /><br />Connor, whose dealt with false rumours too (I mean which one of them haven’t, but still)! Connor!!! Who really almost said those disgusting words to Jane. Why??? How??? Does he not remember when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his marriage was called a sham, and there was every evidence to prove it so? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> How can he really believe this shit?<br /><br />How can ANY of them????? Unrealistic. Fake. It isn’t real you can’t convince me. I’m done! I don’t like this book.<br /><br />Anyway, maybe if I’m in a better mood I’ll edit this and add the very few things I actually loved. <br />Like Charlie Cobalt.<br /><br />Though not to sound too much like Ryke but: I’m fucking disappointed and angry.<br />__________<br /><br />I HAVE SO MUCH TO SAY BUT NOT TODAY. TOMORROW. I AM TIRED. AND THINGS I WILL SAY ARE NOT GOOD ANYWAY SO WHATEVER.<br /><br />p.s can't believe the next one isn't about sulli or jane. looks like the suffering continues ://</span>
  <a data-text-id="13395063944919413979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2042243465?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="*J* Too Many Books Too Little Time" class="user" itemprop="url" name="*J* Too Many Books Too Little Time" href="/user/show/9072385-j-too-many-books-too-little-time">*J* Too Many Books Too Little Time</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35047889-damaged-like-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9072385-j-too-many-books-too-little-time?shelf=male-action">male-action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9072385-j-too-many-books-too-little-time?shelf=liked-a-lot">liked-a-lot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9072385-j-too-many-books-too-little-time?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9072385-j-too-many-books-too-little-time?shelf=dirty-dirty-boy">dirty-dirty-boy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9072385-j-too-many-books-too-little-time?shelf=low-angst">low-angst</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2042243465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7207590407928915433"><b>5 Stars!</b><br/><br/>12/6/2018 - Third time re-reading this one and I am going to go up a star. Farrow and Moffy never get old. Love them. <br/><br/>------------------------------------------------<br/><br/>03/22/2018 - Decided to do a re-read of this one after finishing book 3, which I rarely ever do. And I must say, I enjoyed it just as much the second time! My rating stands at 4.5 Stars!<br/><br/>------------------------------------------------<br/><br/><b>4.5 Stars!</b><br/><br/>Whelp! I liked this one. A lot. <br/><br/>I did read <i>most</i> of the other series. But not all. </span>
  <span id="freeText7207590407928915433" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars!</b><br /><br />12/6/2018 - Third time re-reading this one and I am going to go up a star. Farrow and Moffy never get old. Love them. <br /><br />------------------------------------------------<br /><br />03/22/2018 - Decided to do a re-read of this one after finishing book 3, which I rarely ever do. And I must say, I enjoyed it just as much the second time! My rating stands at 4.5 Stars!<br /><br />------------------------------------------------<br /><br /><b>4.5 Stars!</b><br /><br />Whelp! I liked this one. A lot. <br /><br />I did read <i>most</i> of the other series. But not all. And I did like them at the time. But that was a few years ago, so I honestly wasn't sure how I would feel about this one. <br /><br />And really, after the first chapter or so I wasn't so sure I was going to like it. But then I read a bit more, and then a bit more, and before I knew it I was hooked. <br /><br />It was a very addicting story-line and writing, much like the other series. <br /><br />However, it wasn't perfect. There was a lot of repetitiveness. Especially when it came to descriptions of things. We were told the MCs hair and eye color repeatedly, which got old. <br /><br />Also there really wasn't much plot. It was mostly "a day in the life of a celebrity". But at the same time, I found that aspect entertaining. <br /><br />So for what this was, I enjoyed it. I was entertained. I laughed. It was hot. There was virtually no relationship angst (big plus). The MCs were likable, as were many of the secondary characters. Several of which I hope get their own books and are MM. <br /><br />With that being said, these two characters are slated to get two more books. I am not always a fan of continuing series. This one was a HFN ending but it was a solid ending. One I could be satisfied with whether I continue with the series or not. But as of now, I do plan to continue. <br /><br />This book won't be for everyone. But I'm glad I gave it go.</span>

<div id="review_1237395531" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237395531" />
    <a title="Wil Loves Books!" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3232198-wil-loves-books"><img alt="Wil Loves Books!" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467223384p2/3232198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237395531?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wil Loves Books!" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wil Loves Books!" href="/user/show/3232198-wil-loves-books">Wil Loves Books!</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35047889-damaged-like-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3232198-wil-loves-books?shelf=priority-tbr">priority-tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3232198-wil-loves-books?shelf=not-yet-released">not-yet-released</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3232198-wil-loves-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3232198-wil-loves-books?shelf=mm">mm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237395531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15395552792325461172"><strong>
  <em>“We're like lightning and thunder, inherently different but alike enough to share the same sky.”</em>
</strong><br/><br/>Absolute Perfection! I’m so in love with this book. I know I normally say that when I absolutely love a book I just read but it’s the honest truth! All the love! I’m not sure how I’ll be able to wait until October for Book 2. Now forgive me in advance if I go on tangents or have a few rants on this review. This one is truly special to me.<br/><br/>It’s not a secret I’m a huge fan of the Addicted Series, hug</span>
  <span id="freeText15395552792325461172" style="display:none"><strong>
  <em>“We're like lightning and thunder, inherently different but alike enough to share the same sky.”</em>
</strong><br><br>Absolute Perfection! I’m so in love with this book. I know I normally say that when I absolutely love a book I just read but it’s the honest truth! All the love! I’m not sure how I’ll be able to wait until October for Book 2. Now forgive me in advance if I go on tangents or have a few rants on this review. This one is truly special to me.<br><br>It’s not a secret I’m a huge fan of the Addicted Series, huge. It’s one of my top series ever. It’s also not a secret, if you read my reviews, that this series snuck up on me and took over my heart. I wasn’t an insta-fan. I wasn’t a fan of the first 2 books, they were difficult and hard. But there was still something about them that kept me coming back, something about these characters, they just felt so real. And boy was it worth it, once I got deeper into the story I fell in love with these characters and I knew they would hold a place in my heart forever.<br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>“When you're different from the pack, it takes more guts to be yourself”</em>
</strong><br><br>Where do I begin describing all my feelings while reading this book? The one constant in my mind while reading the book was HAPPY. I was so happy the entire time! Had this huge grin on my face. While this was a little angsty at times, this was overall such a light, beautiful book. If you’ve read the Addicted books, you’ve met the child version of Maximoff (Moffy) Hale, he is Loren and Lily’s son. Let me tell you, Maximoff was everything I was hoping for: beautiful, strong, self-assured, smart, dorky (he’s a Hale!) and caring. Oh, so caring. He is truly Lily and Lo’s son. His love for his family, for his parents, siblings, cousins is everything. My heart was full reading about it. It was also a testament to the great writing of Krista &amp; Becca, and the fact that these characters are so well developed you can’t help but being fully invested in their lives.<br><br>And the romance, oh man the romance part was all sorts of awesome! You see Moffy has grown up in the spotlight. His family has always been in the limelight and now is stronger than ever. He lives no ordinary life and so he requires 24/7 security, as many other high-profile celebrities do. When his teenage crush, Farrow Keene, gets assigned as his bodyguards, it completely changes his life. I guess you need to read to understand why, what type of person Moffy is, what type of family he comes from and why he’s chosen to be so morally correct.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498967238i/23177902._SY540_.jpg" alt="" width="444" height="555" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p>
  <strong>
    <em>“Maximoff Hale is something else, and from start to finish, I can't imagine anyone else having him but me.”</em>
  </strong>
</p><br><br><br>Anyway, Farrow and Moffy are at odds since the beginning. For one, they’re both super alpha. For two, they’re both trying to hide their attraction to each other. I loved the angst and the anticipation.<br><br><br><strong>
  <em>“Most people find Farrow Redford Keene intimidating at first sight, but I'm immune to most kinds of intimidation. It's called being a Hale. I can describe Farrow in three meaningful ways. 1. Frustrating. 2. Aggravating. 3. Piss in my hot tea.”</em>
</strong><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>“If Farrow was pushed to the front, I craved to find a way next to him. If Farrow went fast, I went harder. And he never let up. With anything, he was too headstrong to let me pass without a hard-won fight.”</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br>The sexual tension:<br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>“I stare him directly in the eye. Unabashed, but I keep thinking, never in my goddamn life have I wanted to accept an order like that one as badly as I do now. I'm highly aware that I've always been drawn to alpha males. The kind of men who want to top me as much as I want to top them. I get my way almost every time, but just toying with the vulnerability of being with someone just as strong, just as dominant, lights me up to the fucking max.”</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>“He tenses, breathing shallow, and he looks back at me. He's still only dressed in drawstring pants, his ass literal perfection in them. I've never wanted to touch, hold and fuck someone as much as I want to touch, hold and fuck him. And even though I just massaged Maximoff, it still feels like not enough. Not nearly enough.”</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>“I try to master restraint, but my eyes say what my mouth can’t. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>Kiss me. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>He reads them. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>I know he reads them, and our chests collapse and rise in heavy unison. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>Jesus Christ. I can't. We can't. But I think, fucking kiss me. Just do it.”</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br>And the banter!<br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>I swig my orange juice before saying, "Look what the wind threw up." I set down my glass. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>Farrow raises his apple to his mouth. "You mean blew in. " </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>"No," I say firmly, palms on the pearly counter. "I meant threw up."</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>"Thank you for that technical adjustment." </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>"Anytime, wolf scout." He eases forward and lowers his voice to the sexiest whisper, "It's good to remember that I'm better than you at most everything."</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>It takes a lot of effort not to stare at his mouth. "Sounds like an alternate universe." </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>One corner of his lip quirks, and then he eases back. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>Boom.</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br>I’m completely in love with Farrow! I thought he was definitely the right fit for Moffy. The only one that could tame him, and the one who could keep up. They’re equals and opposites all at the same time. A perfect match! Moffy’s description of him is perfect:<br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>“Somewhere around my sixteenth birthday, I started crushing on him. Maybe it's because he never just gives me the win. Maybe it's that he's five years older and a Yale graduate. Or that he does thirty pull-ups like it's a damn breeze. Maybe it's all the gray and black tattoos that cover his fair skin, even to his throat. Beautiful inked symmetric wings decorate his neck, crossed swords on his Adam's apple. Maybe it's his four visible piercings: a hoop on his nostril, bottom lip, and two barbells on his brow. Maybe it's all of that combined together that heats my skin, pools blood south, and attracts me like an idiot. He's made permanent camp in my cerebral cortex and cock, and I don't know how to extract him.”</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498967238i/23177903._SY540_.jpg" alt="" width="600" height="600" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br><p>
  <strong>
    <em>“Everything about Farrow is lightning cracking the night sky”</em>
  </strong>
</p><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br>And his feelings for Moffy are so real, and so raw:<br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>“His love for his siblings toughens him, not softens. And a guy being so protective over the people he loves, I find extremely fucking sexy.”</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>"We can't all be heroes," I say matter-of-factly. His glare falls to me, but his lips inch bit by bit, our arms still hooked tight around each other. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><strong>
  <em>"If I'm not the hero, what am I?" </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>Maximoff is waiting for me to call him a villain. In his comic books, that's the dichotomy. Heroes versus villains. He's very far from one. I press my lips to his jaw, his neck, and against his ear, I whisper, "You're a prince who wants to be a knight."</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>"And I tell him bluntly, assuredly, without a fucking doubt, "You're my boyfriend. And from the jump-start, this has always been more than just sex."</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br>Ok, I need to stop! I don't want to spoil the story and I really want you to read it, But that’s the thing, I can’t  stop. I have so many feelings, and so many highlighted quotes I just want to share them all, cause they’re so gorgeous! I lived for the romance in this book.<br><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498967238ra/23177904.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>Anyway, the book explores romance from a different perspective. Maximoff’s fame is a real issue and it plays a central part in how he’s chosen to live his life.<br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>“Our fame burns. And burns. None of us need to stoke the flames for it to stay lit. And me—fame is my friend and foe. It's a part of me. A tangible thing that lives inside of me. This is the only life I've ever lived. It's the only life I know.”</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br>Because of this Moffy has chosen a life of one-night stands, instead of pursuing a relationship.<br><br><strong>
  <em>"I'll never be in a relationship," he tells me flat-out. "I'll never experience any kind of romance beyond a one-time hookup. Because once I date someone in public, media will hound them to the point of intrusion, vulnerability—I won't ever subject someone to an extreme loss of privacy that they'll never get back. I've accepted that this is my life, and I'm satisfied with that." </em>
</strong><br><br><br><br>That is, until Farrow comes along.<br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>“I'm watched and observed all the time. By strangers. By cameramen. By people. And never, never have I come undone. Until now, until his eyes feel like hands, and I want them all over me.”</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498967238ra/23177905.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>
  <em>“I want to do more. I want more. In a way that I've never even had before, and is that what's being offered? Is it even possible?”</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>“I've never felt breathless in my life. I've never been with anyone I've known. Not like this. Never have I had real feelings beyond physical attraction. Not until him.”</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br>Because Farrow is his bodyguard, and because he’s in such proximity to him 24/7. He feels like he finally can explore those feelings. And when he realizes what he could have in his life, it’s simply amazing!<br><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498967238ra/23177906.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>
  <em>“So this is what it's like, huh? I can kiss someone the next morning. I can expect to see them in an hour. I can do it all again and again. Something lightens in my chest. Feels like freedom.”</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>“He knows me well.</em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em> Millions of people know me, but not like this. Not like that. I hang onto that fact like rope on a wall that blocks my view of everything. He's how I see the other side. He's made my life feel freer. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>He made me believe I could actually have a relationship. He made me believe I could experience more than just this fleeting, temporary thing. </em>
</strong><br><br><strong>
  <em>And I have."</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498967238i/23177907.jpg" alt="" width="537" height="361" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p>
  <strong>
    <em>“This is what I missed in my life, and I can't imagine never discovering this feeling. Never having him.”</em>
  </strong>
</p><br><strong>
  <em> </em>
</strong><br><br>This book is beautiful, hot and extremely romantic. It also explores things like fame, family and privacy. I also love how gutsy Krista and Becca were when exploring some themes in here, I definitely didn’t find anything out of character or was surprised by anything. I also think that this was amazingly written MM. I’m no-nonsense when it comes to these things. I read lots of books every year, a lot of them are MM. I’ve read MM by established MM authors and there are some I haven’t liked. Similarly, I’ve read MM by established MF authors and I’ve loved them. So I make no distinction when it comes to a good writer. A good writer is a good writer and a good book is a good book. I don’t immediately discard a book because the writer “typically” writes a different genre and so on. This was just perfect. The more I read Krista &amp; Becca Ritchie, the more I fall in love with their books, their impeccable writing and their attention to detail.<br><br><br><br>Damaged Like Us ends on a happy note, but it's still Book 1 on a series, there will be more than one book. This can be read as a separate series from the Addicted Series although it's a spin-off. The authors have gone above and beyond to explain everything where the new reader won’t feel so lost. However, I think that your experience with this story would be so much better if you’ve read the Addicted Series. Or maybe, I just selfishly want everyone to read those awesome books!<br><br><br><br>Ok, I’m finally done now with my essay. I absolutely recommend this book, from the bottom of my heart. I can’t wait for book 2 and all the books in this series. There’s so much more to explore, so many unanswered questions and so much to look forward to! I especially want to know about Janie and Sully and their love interests! Needless to say, I’m a fangirl for these books and also a #proudweirdo. Bring it on K&amp;B! I’ll be waiting! If you hung on till the end, thanks a lot! 100% recommend Damaged Like Us<br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498967238i/23177908._SY540_.jpg" alt="" width="485" height="604" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><strong>
  <em>"I hoped for someone who wasn't afraid to put me in my place, someone who made me feel human. I hoped for someone who could be strong so I could be vulnerable, but still never make me feel weak or less than. I hoped for trust and understanding and an innate love of my family. And I realized, Farrow..." His hand slides up my neck to my jaw, his welling eyes already caressing mine. "I realized," I breathe, "that I was always hoping and wishing for you." Say the words. "I'm in love with you, and I'm the lucky one here."</em>
</strong><br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444752880i/16547832.png" alt="" width="200" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <br><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498967238i/23177909._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="800" height="600" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br> <strong>Buy it Here: <a href="http://amzn.to/2t4wSNI" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2tDipdi" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon CA</a> / <a href="http://amzn.to/2sem2lp" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a> </strong>/<a href="http://apple.co/2rAWa7m" rel="nofollow noopener"> iBooks</a> <br><br><br><strong>JOIN THE SISTERHOOD! FIND US ON: </strong><strong><a href="https://www.facebook.com/tbbsisterhood" rel="nofollow noopener">FACEBOOK</a> / <a href="https://www.instagram.com/tbbsisterhood" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a> / <a href="https://twitter.com/tbbsisterhood" rel="nofollow noopener">TWITTER</a> / <a href="http://tbbsisterhood.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">BLOG</a></strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="15395552792325461172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText9524415578009147908" style="display:none"><b>3.75 Stars</b><br /><br />Surprisingly I enjoyed this book! I said surprisingly because it hadn't a real/strong plot! It’s more about Maximoff’s siblings and his cousins, their relationships, their problems, and insecurities. But nothing special about Maximoff and Farrow’s relationship! I mean everything between them was simple! They just did their daily routines and enjoyed being with each other. and for the lack of the actual plot, it seems slow! But what can I say?! I was in the mood and enjoyed it! both characters were likable and I liked their banter! Not just MCs, but all the secondary characters were likable! I liked their relationship with each other and how Maximoffs were protective of them and Farrow of him!<br /><br />Told in dual POV, 1st person. It’s the first installment in the "Like Us" series. Even though it doesn’t end on a cliffhanger the second installment is also about them and I hope it gets better! All in all, I really liked this one and hope you enjoy it as well!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508507159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12232115678849002015"><b>*** Only 99c ***</b><br/><br/><b>Disclaimer: This is incredibly long... my bad, and I didn't proofread so if something doesn't make sense, again... my bad lol ;)</b><br/><br/>I fangirled like CRAZY when I found out this spin-off series (which can be read separately from the Addicted/Calloway books) was happening!! This shouldn't be too surprising since I'm OBSESSED with these authors and <b>everything</b> they write!!!! But I was beyond excited for Moffy and Farrow's story!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475988021ra/20789949.gif' width='350' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452501262ra/17699325.gif' width='350' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Truthfully, I wasn't sure what to expect from this. I assume</span>
  <span id="freeText12232115678849002015" style="display:none"><b>*** Only 99c ***</b><br><br><b>Disclaimer: This is incredibly long... my bad, and I didn't proofread so if something doesn't make sense, again... my bad lol ;)</b><br><br>I fangirled like CRAZY when I found out this spin-off series (which can be read separately from the Addicted/Calloway books) was happening!! This shouldn't be too surprising since I'm OBSESSED with these authors and <b>everything</b> they write!!!! But I was beyond excited for Moffy and Farrow's story!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475988021ra/20789949.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452501262ra/17699325.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Truthfully, I wasn't sure what to expect from this. I assumed it was going to be emotional like the Addicted and Calloway Sisters series were, but it ended up not being like that at all. And while that's not a bad thing, I definitely did miss that aspect. Mainly because I think these authors have such an amazing talent for writing those gut-wrenching scenes. But that's not to say I was disappointed because, as it turns out, they write comedy really well too! There were funny moments in their other books, but nothing like this. I honestly wasn't expecting this to be as funny as it was...<blockquote>
  <i>"She has FOMEFT." Fear of Missing Every Fucking Thing.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>Dear World, stop fucking with me. Sincerely, an agitated human.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>Picturing a polar bear eating Fritos on the moon is easier than imagining Farrow as my bodyguard.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>"Cool," I say as he passes me my phone. Yeah, so cool. Let my childhood-crush-also-turned-bodyguard pick out my lube for me. That will make not fantasizing about him so much easier. So smart of me. Genius. Maybe I shouldn't have dropped out of Harvard.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>"It's a Cobalt thing... they have a harder time knowing when to shut up."</i>
</blockquote>Or for there to be so much delicious banter between Moffy and Farrow...<blockquote>
  <i>"You also have another typo."<br>"Shut up about the fucking typos," I say and adjust the air conditioner, my body hot as his smile stretches wider and wider.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>"Because [my abs] are better, wolf scout." He huffs, then glares and motions to me. "Take off your shirt and we'll find out."</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>"Which one of you made the first move anyway?"<br>"Me," Farrow and I say in unison.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>"I could've sworn the bet was to make me hard, not want to push you out of the car."</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500921830ra/23396365.gif" width="450" height="325" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I LOVED the comedic side of this book, but they also had sweet moments...<blockquote>
  <i>He adjusts the air vents and points the ice-cold at me. I glance from him to the road. "You cold?" I can adjust the air for him.<br>He types on my notepad app. "You looked hot."</i>
</blockquote>This was such a small and simple moment, but I loved what it represented! It showed just how in tune they are to one another, how they're constantly thinking about the other person over themselves. Their relationship in general was amazing. I loved that they were two alpha males, it made it so entertaining! And somehow it felt different than the other MM novels I've read. Maybe it was the banter? Maybe it was the security aspect and potential danger? Or the constant need to one-up the other? Whatever it was—it worked. I don't feel like I've ever read about a relationship like theirs before. I'm not sure if that makes sense... but their alpha tendencies felt unique, and I can safely say Moffy &amp; Farrow are my favorite MM couple ever!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494886191ra/22762624.gif" width="500" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>- Moffy -</b><br><br>Oh man, how I loved him! There were a lot of things to admire, but first and foremost was his dedication to his family, especially his parents. Lily &amp; Lo (*heart eyes*) have not had an easy road and Moffy knows it. But he sees so much more than the negative.<blockquote>
  <i>They're my heroes. And I'm damn proud to be their son.</i>
</blockquote>And he tries to do this for everyone in his family. Farrow is exactly right when says...<blockquote>
  <i>Moffy tries to be everything for everyone.</i>
</blockquote>At times Moffy might come across as a goody-two shoes and seem a bit unreal, but I never felt that way. He just genuinely wants what is best for everyone, and I think as the oldest (male) child, he feels like it's his responsibility to give it to them.<blockquote>
  <i>What's right anymore? I'm searching for the sword that I need to fall on. I just don't want to hurt Jane or Farrow in the process. I can't hurt him. I can't.</i>
</blockquote>He's the type to bottle up his feelings, to hide his pain in order to shoulder someone else's, and knowing these sisters, I don't doubt we'll see him blow up at one point or another. And I'm kind of hoping it'll be at the paparazzi. He's a good sport about most of it. He even says, if he didn't look at it the way he does he'd <i>"be irritated every minute of every single day."</i> Because they're just so commonplace in his world, through no fault of Moffy's or any of the kids. All the fame is leftover and borrowed, but it affects the children all the same. And I think it bothers Moffy more than he lets on.<blockquote>
  <i>Our fame burns. And burns. None of us need to stoke the flames for it to stay lit.</i>
</blockquote>I have no doubt that we'll see that Moffy's selflessness has ended up costing him something. Everyone has a flaw, and his just might lie in his strength. I think there's a lot of development left for his character, despite the fact that he seems so solid, and I'm really looking forward to it! Character development is what these authors do best ;)<br><br>*Side note: There were times when one might think the mentions of his family and/or the media were OTT, but that's because that's how Moffy's life is. It would be disingenuous if he wasn't constantly thinking about and/or referring to these things.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500931046ra/23397250.gif" width="450" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>- Farrow -</b><br><br>We don't learn much about him in this one. But what we've learned, I LOVE! He has such a great attitude, plus having him "tattooed and pierced" certainly never hurts ;) One of my favorite aspects was his take on the "forbidden" romance.<blockquote>
  <i>In my head, I can be his bodyguard and sleep with him. I'm that good. And it's that simple.</i>
</blockquote>Granted, some of this is being conceited, but a big part of it is Farrow's morality. I feel like Moffy's morality is discussed a lot, but no one says much about Farrow's. Their moralities are very different, and yet they are both good people. And I think it will interesting to see how this all plays out in the next novel. Because Moffy is a rule-follower, and Farrow is admittedly not. He lives by his own sense of right and wrong, something I personally appreciate because I don't subscribe to the idea that just because someone more powerful made a rule that that automatically makes it "right."<blockquote>
  <i>"How about rewinding and asking yourself, is it really wrong? Or how about this one: what is ethical to begin with? Who decided on these moral rights?"</i>
</blockquote>So when he said that ^^ I just about died. If I hadn't already been in love with him before that, that certainly would have made me fall. I'm SO excited to learn more about him.<br><br>*Side note: While I love that Farrow broke the mold and didn't care, it also lost some of the forbidden appeal, in my opinion. That didn't bother me because I'm not obsessed with forbidden romances, but it did leave me a bit confused because I didn't completely understand why it was more forbidden for Moffy than Farrow. I guess I never fully understood Moffy's reasoning for thinking it was wrong. Maybe it's because my sense of morality aligns more with Farrow, but it felt a little strange to me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500931046ra/23397251.gif" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>- The Ending -</b><br><br>I know this was a big deal for a lot of people and I wanted to give my two cents, but it is a MAJOR spoiler. So don't click unless you really want to know...<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I actually liked it. I know many didn't, which I could understand, and there were a few minor plot holes that I wish had been addressed, but it was a unique conflict and I really appreciated that it was atypical.<br><br>So the book ends with the core six believing a rumor that Jane and Moffy are sleeping together. Ew, right? I don't have many hard limits, but incest is one of them. Except Jane and Moffy AREN'T ACTUALLY SLEEPING TOGETHER! So I'm not sure why the "possibility" was even floated (in reviews and critiques, I mean). Actually, I do know why. It's because they're very close. BUT, and this a big but, this is another reason why I liked the ending. If Moffy had been Luna, THIS WOULDN'T EVEN BE AN ISSUE.<br><br>I find the notion that a guy and girl can't be close friends without falling for each other completely absurd. And this doesn't even take into account the actual <i>people</i> involved. It makes complete sense (to me, at least) why Moffy and Jane would be so close. They're the two oldest children, separated by only a few months, in a family that is constantly shoved in the public eye. No one would understand this pressure, this scrutiny better than the two of them. Plus, since it's so difficult to tell who from the outside world is being genuine, relying on each other for support is tantamount to survival for Moffy and Jane. So I loved and completely understood their close relationship.<br><br>Now, to the rumor and the parents disbelief...<br><br>I know many were upset that the parents didn't believe Moffy and Jane, I was too, but I also understood it. I think it's supposed to be hard to swallow. Because we love the core six, too. We idolize them a bit, just like Moffy. It's supposed to <i>hurt</i>.<br><br>*Side note: I remember there were times when I was reading Rose's POV and I didn't like Lo all the time, because I was seeing him through Rose's eyes. And that's how this works. It's easy to love and understand someone when you have all their thoughts, but it will always be harder to see through someone else.<br><br>Back to the point... If you've ever been in a household where addictions are present and people constantly <i>lie</i> about those addictions, it becomes very hard to trust people. You question everything, you question simple things. I've had experience with this and it's not fun. No one wants to believe their loved one is lying to them, it physically <i>pains</i> family members to feel this way. But more often than not, we've been burned too many times. That's just the nature of addiction in families, and it's a lifelong thing because addiction is a lifelong struggle. There is no end and there is no magic button that lets you fully trust that person again.<br><br>I think we all would like to believe we'd 100% trust our kids if the situation were reversed, and I truly think they might have if Farrow hadn't declared that Moffy was in a relationship with a forbidden woman. I think <i>this</i> fueled a lot of their skepticism. (And I actually liked this too, I don't think it was stupid of Farrow, because what else could he really say?)<br><br>Jane hit the nail on the freaking head with this quote...<blockquote><i>"We did nothing to lose their trust. They projected their own pasts onto us like the media always does, and they should've never doubted us."</i></blockquote>*Claps* *Bows* *Screams "hallelujah"*<br><br>No, they shouldn't have doubted them. But projection is a very real thing. It's why cheating spouses always assume their partner is also cheating on them. We see the world how <i>we</i> are. So I understood their doubts (all except Daisy, I sort of wish she'd been more vocal because I think of everyone she would have given them the benefit of the doubt). They weren't thinking about their children necessarily, but themselves. At the same time, I don't understand why they'd trust a tabloid over them though. Moffy is spot-on when he says...<blockquote><i>People don't like to believe facts. They want to believe the most salacious story. The one that makes you keep flipping the pages. That story isn't always the truth.</i></blockquote>Maybe if it had been a different source, I'd feel differently. But knowing what they know, with how tabloids tried to tear them down through the years, it felt a stretch that they would trust <i>that</i> source.<br><br>Regardless, I also believe this will go a long way in Moffy's development. He's always worshiped his father, but Lo isn't perfect and Moffy needed to see that. It's definitely going to be painful to watch.<blockquote><i>I prepared myself to deal with tabloids, the world. Not my family. And while you may think the world would be a worse battle—it's not.</i></blockquote>I'm really looking forward to how the dynamic between Moffy and his parents change. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>So why not 5 stars?</b><br><br>For most of the book I felt like romance was secondary. I didn't mind so much because I love this entire cast of characters and I wanted to catch up with all of them, but newcomers *might* feel overwhelmed. I wouldn't discourage any one from reading this, just prepare yourself for a lot of people.<br><br>At the same time, it's hard to imagine how the sisters could have done it any differently because these people are essential to Moffy's life. So it's hard to be critical when I can't pinpoint what should have been different, I just personally felt like I was missing a little something from the romance.<br><br>I'm not concerned about the rest of the series though. I definitely enjoyed this and would recommend it. I think this was just a tough first book to write, trying to balance the previous series while making it readable for a new audience. And even though I wanted a bit more from Moffy and Farrow, I know it'll come later and it's hard not to be impressed with this one because I think between the pressure and the lengthy cast it was probably a very challenging book to write.<br><br>A few final quotes because I'm me...<blockquote>
  <i>We're like lightning and thunder, inherently different but alike enough to share the same sky.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>My lips meet his lips, and the tension explodes. We thrust forward together. An invisible divide detonates, blown to pieces.</i>
</blockquote><blockquote>
  <i>"I was always hoping and wishing for you... I'm in love with you, and I'm the lucky one here."</i>
</blockquote>But MY GOD! I need the other stories!! I need, like physically NEED Jane and Thatcher to be a thing *prays hard* Also I'm partial to Akara for Sulli, and I can't wait for that story line either... <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1500931707ra/23397302.gif" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Safety: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Moffy and Farrow have known each other for years, with Moffy crushing on Farrow when he was sixteen. So they have seen each other in other relationships. But as with every KBR book, once they are together, they're <i><b>together.</b></i><blockquote><i>"You need to know that I only do exclusive. No fucking around. You want me, you only get me, and vice versa."</i></blockquote>*sigh* I love Farrow!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Closure: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[HFN. Their story continues in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21428058.Lovers_like_Us__Like_Us___2_" title="Lovers like Us (Like Us, #2) by Krista Ritchie" rel="nofollow noopener">Lovers Like Us</a> &lt;3 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047751708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18281307298984414530">The realease date for <i>Lovers Like US</i> is so close that I had to reread this once more before diving into the sequel. I'm so happy I did that because I forgot a lot of small details. I think it goes without saying that this book was just delightful and enchanting all over again! I think I loved it this second time around even more than the first. Farrow and Maximoff have burrowed themselves into my heart. I kind of want to reread this book again. Would that be overkill? <br/><br/>---<br/><br/>GURLLLLLLLL! <br/>This is def</span>
  <span id="freeText18281307298984414530" style="display:none">The realease date for <i>Lovers Like US</i> is so close that I had to reread this once more before diving into the sequel. I'm so happy I did that because I forgot a lot of small details. I think it goes without saying that this book was just delightful and enchanting all over again! I think I loved it this second time around even more than the first. Farrow and Maximoff have burrowed themselves into my heart. I kind of want to reread this book again. Would that be overkill? <br /><br />---<br /><br />GURLLLLLLLL! <br />This is definitely beyond what I was expecting this book to be! It exceeded my really high expectations. This was my first M/M romance and I think that it was amazing. I felt like the story was well structured, and it included not only Maximoff's siblings and cousins, but also int othe world of the bodyguards. This was everything that the Ritchie Sisters promised and more in my opinion. There wasn't a lot of LiLo, Coballoway, or Raisy, but there presence was definitely there. Also, I have predictions for the sequel already, which by the way, I'm really excited about. I need <i>Lovers Like Us</i> like <b>right now</b>. I legit love this book with all my heart! <br /><br />I will be doing a video review on <i>Damaged Like Us</i> soon. In which I will be going into more detail about everything that encompasses this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18281307298984414530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2043277500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2043277500" />
    <a title="Sabrina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18085807-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392065462p2/18085807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2043277500?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina" href="/user/show/18085807-sabrina">Sabrina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2043615162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11053617962695868951"><b>5 GUARD MY BODY STARS!!!</b><br/><br/>I need to read the books about these young'uns parents. I'm pretty sure they are in the black hole that is my kindle drowning with all the other books that have been waiting patiently to be picked as my next read. (I really need to organize that thing) This happens to be my first book by these authors. I KNOW! But I will definitely move the parent books up on my TBR. <br/><br/>Now, about this book...<br/><br/>I really liked it. It was funny, sexy, and had a lot of fun characters that I loved</span>
  <span id="freeText11053617962695868951" style="display:none"><b>5 GUARD MY BODY STARS!!!</b><br /><br />I need to read the books about these young'uns parents. I'm pretty sure they are in the black hole that is my kindle drowning with all the other books that have been waiting patiently to be picked as my next read. (I really need to organize that thing) This happens to be my first book by these authors. I KNOW! But I will definitely move the parent books up on my TBR. <br /><br />Now, about this book...<br /><br />I really liked it. It was funny, sexy, and had a lot of fun characters that I loved getting to know and hope will have books in the future. But lets focus on the two MC's of this one for now. I really liked them both. They had really great chemistry and their banter was very entertaining. I enjoyed the build up and then the explosion of their sexy times. I liked how protective they were of each other. <br /><br />Maximoff Hale was born into one of the most famous families and has been a celebrity since birth. He has very little privacy but handles his stardom like a boss. He's very headstrong and stubborn in his ways. He has also had his own bodyguard since he was born. The same bodyguard. That is until that bodyguard decides to retire and he is being assigned a new one. Maximoff isn't happy about it at all. He's not good with change and the unknown. He likes to be in control and is feeling quite off balance when his new bodyguard steps through the doors. Because it's his worse nightmare and wet dream come true all at once. Farrow Keene. From the moment he is on page with Moffy you feel the chemistry these two men have come off the screen (in my case at least). You also feel the tension of their attraction. Maximoff and Keene do a bit of a dance around each other, but once their attraction is made known by one another, all bets and clothes are off and a relationship starts to be built. But it's not easy and they have to keep their budding romance on the DL because if their relationship is found out that means Keene will lose his job and Moffy will find himself with another bodyguard and neither wants that to happen. <br /><br />There is so much that happens in this book and it would be spoilery to mention much more of it. Just read it! lol<br /><br />This is a great start to what I know will end up being a great series. I can't wait for the next one! <br /><br />Happy reading dolls! xx<br /><br /> </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1144947172" />
    <a title="Betül" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4954296-bet-l"><img alt="Betül" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516360322p2/4954296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1144947172?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betül" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betül" href="/user/show/4954296-bet-l">Betül</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4954296-bet-l?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4954296-bet-l?shelf=2017-favs">2017-favs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4954296-bet-l?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4954296-bet-l?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4954296-bet-l?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4954296-bet-l?shelf=mm">mm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1144947172" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer936471569118517572"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473099653i/20407729.jpg' width='400' height='100' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Damaged Like Us is the perfect first book in the new Like Us series. I had very high expectations and Krista and Becca met all of them with this book. With many new series, there often is a huge amount of information being thrown around in the first book (which can be confusing at times). However, I was really happy with the way the authors handled everything. There are many new characters, but they were introduced in a very smooth way. Right from the beginning I was looking forward to catching </span>
  <span id="freeText936471569118517572" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1473099653i/20407729.jpg" width="400" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Damaged Like Us is the perfect first book in the new Like Us series. I had very high expectations and Krista and Becca met all of them with this book. With many new series, there often is a huge amount of information being thrown around in the first book (which can be confusing at times). However, I was really happy with the way the authors handled everything. There are many new characters, but they were introduced in a very smooth way. Right from the beginning I was looking forward to catching up with the Addicted series characters (I love them so much), however the kids, who the focus will be on in this series, stole my heart. Each and every one of them are so unique and awesome. I just can't wait to get to know them better. <br><br>Damaged Like Us focuses on Maximoff (Moffy) and his new bodyguard Farrow. I just loved their banter so much. Also the attraction was off the chain! This book was everything! It was emotional at times, hilarious, sad, SEXY and so much more. The make-out and sex scenes got me all hot and bothered (which doesn't happen that often). But there was just something special about Moffy and Farrow's chemistry. I just love that Krista and Becca take the time to really develop the story and characters. Both were done perfectly and I wouldn't change a thing. I also adore Moffy and Jane's relationship. I am dying to get my hands on the next book. If you love unique plots and characters, and love to be surprised then I highly recommend this book. Krista and Becca will take you on a beautiful, emotional, funny, but also rocky journey. The authors are one of my all time favorites, and I will read anything they'll write. </span>
  <a data-text-id="936471569118517572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
